Hey ... now that looks promissing :-) &#010;&#010;I'll give that a spin as soon as I have time.&#010;&#010;I didn't know that you could use variables in the scope (But I think that's just some old&#010;info probably stored in my brain ages ago).&#010;&#010;Chris&#010;&#010;&#010;________________________________________&#010;Von: Jörg Schaible &lt;joerg.schaible@gmx.de&gt;&#010;Gesendet: Sonntag, 29. Juni 2014 15:16&#010;An: users@maven.apache.org&#010;Betreff: Re: AW: AW: Artifact with different sets of dependencies switched by profiles&#010;&#010;Hi Christoper,&#010;&#010;Christofer Dutz wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi Ron,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I think you got what I'm trying to do a little wrong. It's not two&#010;&gt; different set of dependencies, it's two different ways of linking the same&#010;&gt; set of libraries. If I were to translate this into java, imagine that the&#010;&gt; default way an application was built would be to include all Classes&#010;&gt; needed by the application to be bundled in the application Jar (The&#010;&gt; classes not needed aren't included). Now in modular applications I am able&#010;&gt; to switch to something exactly the same as in Java ... no code is included&#010;&gt; in the Application jar, but the referenced libraries are deployed in&#010;&gt; parallel to the application jar, so the JVM can pull them in as needed (In&#010;&gt; Flex this type is called rsl (runtime shared library).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So in principal I have the same set of dependencies, but in the&#010;&gt; rsl-linking type these dependencies have an additional "scope=rsl"&#010;&gt; setting. Up until now there was only one pom with the default set of&#010;&gt; dependencies. If the users wanted to utilize rsl linking they would have&#010;&gt; to manually add each dependency and set that's scope to rsl. I would like&#010;&gt; to make it easier for users to switch.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So the profiles is bad, the pom with classifier doesn't work ... I would&#010;&gt; really like to avoid to have something like an "flramework" artifact and&#010;&gt; one "framework-rsl" for the rsl linking.&#010;&#010;What's the default value for the scope? "compile"? Then you can do all you&#010;need with properties. You might use a profile, but it is not necessary:&#010;&#010;Declare your dependencies just like before (either in depMgmt or directly):&#010;&#010;============== %&lt; =================&#010; &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;   &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.flex.framework&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;   &lt;artifactId&gt;spark&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;   &lt;version&gt;4.12.1.20140427&lt;/version&gt;&#010;   &lt;type&gt;swc&lt;/type&gt;&#010;   &lt;scope&gt;${flexmojo.scope}&lt;/scope&gt;&#010; &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010; ...&#010; &lt;properties&gt;&#010;   &lt;flexmojo.scope&gt;compile&lt;/flexmojo.scope&gt;&#010; &lt;/properties&gt;&#010;============== %&lt; =================&#010;&#010;Then you can simply redefine "flexmojo.scope" from command line. This will&#010;also affect inherited dependencies, if they are declared in the same way in&#010;the repository or if you delcare them in a common parent with a&#010;dependencyManagement section. You might even overwrite the property in a&#010;profile:&#010;&#010;============== %&lt; =================&#010; &lt;profile&gt;&#010;   &lt;id&gt;rsl&lt;/id&gt;&#010;   &lt;properties&gt;&#010;     &lt;flexmojo.scope&gt;rsl&lt;/flexmojo.scope&gt;&#010;   &lt;/properties&gt;&#010; &lt;profile&gt;&#010;============== %&lt; =================&#010;&#010;Unfortunately, I don't know nothing about flexmojo. If it works like in the&#010;world of C where I can use the same libraries (.lib files) to link an&#010;application either static or dynamically (then requiring runtime libs as&#010;well), then it is possible to do this. Therefore is is fine for an project&#010;creating such an application at the end of a build chain.&#010;&#010;However, if the libraries differ if build with rsl or not, then you will&#010;create a very bad user experience, because - just as Stephen already said -&#010;the build process will use whatever it finds in the local repository, it&#010;cannot separate between artifacts built with rsl or without. Your users&#010;might get a wild mix during build time.&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;Jörg&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

And you are going to have the exact same set of issues as with profiles.&#010;&#010;Maven 3 does not re-interpolate the poms of dependencies IIRC... or at&#010;least it is not supposed to... so you only get to control the variables&#010;from the parent pom and any inherited dependencies/dependencyManagement not&#010;from the transitive dependencies of your pom&#010;&#010;&#010;On 1 July 2014 10:42, Christofer Dutz &lt;christofer.dutz@c-ware.de&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hey ... now that looks promissing :-)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I'll give that a spin as soon as I have time.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I didn't know that you could use variables in the scope (But I think&#010;&gt; that's just some old info probably stored in my brain ages ago).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Chris&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ________________________________________&#010;&gt; Von: Jörg Schaible &lt;joerg.schaible@gmx.de&gt;&#010;&gt; Gesendet: Sonntag, 29. Juni 2014 15:16&#010;&gt; An: users@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; Betreff: Re: AW: AW: Artifact with different sets of dependencies switched&#010;&gt; by profiles&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Hi Christoper,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Christofer Dutz wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Hi Ron,&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I think you got what I'm trying to do a little wrong. It's not two&#010;&gt; &gt; different set of dependencies, it's two different ways of linking the&#010;&gt; same&#010;&gt; &gt; set of libraries. If I were to translate this into java, imagine that the&#010;&gt; &gt; default way an application was built would be to include all Classes&#010;&gt; &gt; needed by the application to be bundled in the application Jar (The&#010;&gt; &gt; classes not needed aren't included). Now in modular applications I am&#010;&gt; able&#010;&gt; &gt; to switch to something exactly the same as in Java ... no code is&#010;&gt; included&#010;&gt; &gt; in the Application jar, but the referenced libraries are deployed in&#010;&gt; &gt; parallel to the application jar, so the JVM can pull them in as needed&#010;&gt; (In&#010;&gt; &gt; Flex this type is called rsl (runtime shared library).&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; So in principal I have the same set of dependencies, but in the&#010;&gt; &gt; rsl-linking type these dependencies have an additional "scope=rsl"&#010;&gt; &gt; setting. Up until now there was only one pom with the default set of&#010;&gt; &gt; dependencies. I would like&#010;&gt; &gt; to make it easier for users to switch.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; So the profiles is bad, the pom with classifier doesn't work ... I would&#010;&gt; &gt; really like to avoid to have something like an "flramework" artifact and&#010;&gt; &gt; one "framework-rsl" for the rsl linking.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; What's the default value for the scope? "compile"? Then you can do all you&#010;&gt; need with properties. You might use a profile, but it is not necessary:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Declare your dependencies just like before (either in depMgmt or directly):&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ============== %&lt; =================&#010;&gt;  &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;&gt;    &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.flex.framework&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;    &lt;artifactId&gt;spark&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;    &lt;version&gt;4.12.1.20140427&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&gt;    &lt;type&gt;swc&lt;/type&gt;&#010;&gt;    &lt;scope&gt;${flexmojo.scope}&lt;/scope&gt;&#010;&gt;  &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&gt;  ...&#010;&gt;  &lt;properties&gt;&#010;&gt;    &lt;flexmojo.scope&gt;compile&lt;/flexmojo.scope&gt;&#010;&gt;  &lt;/properties&gt;&#010;&gt; ============== %&lt; =================&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Then you can simply redefine "flexmojo.scope" from command line. This will&#010;&gt; also affect inherited dependencies, if they are declared in the same way in&#010;&gt; the repository or if you delcare them in a common parent with a&#010;&gt; dependencyManagement section. You might even overwrite the property in a&#010;&gt; profile:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ============== %&lt; =================&#010;&gt;  &lt;profile&gt;&#010;&gt;    &lt;id&gt;rsl&lt;/id&gt;&#010;&gt;    &lt;properties&gt;&#010;&gt;      &lt;flexmojo.scope&gt;rsl&lt;/flexmojo.scope&gt;&#010;&gt;    &lt;/properties&gt;&#010;&gt;  &lt;profile&gt;&#010;&gt; ============== %&lt; =================&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Unfortunately, I don't know nothing about flexmojo. If it works like in the&#010;&gt; world of C where I can use the same libraries (.lib files) to link an&#010;&gt; application either static or dynamically (then requiring runtime libs as&#010;&gt; well), then it is possible to do this. Therefore is is fine for an project&#010;&gt; creating such an application at the end of a build chain.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; However, if the libraries differ if build with rsl or not, then you will&#010;&gt; create a very bad user experience, because - just as Stephen already said -&#010;&gt; the build process will use whatever it finds in the local repository, it&#010;&gt; cannot separate between artifacts built with rsl or without. Your users&#010;&gt; might get a wild mix during build time.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Cheers,&#010;&gt; Jörg&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Hi Stephen,&#010;&#010;Stephen Connolly wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; And you are going to have the exact same set of issues as with profiles.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Maven 3 does not re-interpolate the poms of dependencies IIRC... or at&#010;&gt; least it is not supposed to... so you only get to control the variables&#010;&gt; from the parent pom and any inherited dependencies/dependencyManagement&#010;&gt; not from the transitive dependencies of your pom&#010;&#010;The scope declared in the (inherited) dependencyManagement will overwrite &#010;any transitive or local one (if not explicitly declared). And if that scope &#010;is defined by a property, you may overwrite this property in the local pom &#010;or from command line.&#010;&#010;However, if the resulting intermediate artifacts differ, he will run in &#010;problems.&#010;&#010;- Jörg&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
[ANN] Apache Maven Invoker Plugin 1.9 Released  
Date  :-
Tue, 01 Jul 2014 18:04:21 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the &#010;Apache Maven Invoker Plugin, version 1.9.&#010;&#010;The Invoker Plugin is used to run a set of Maven projects. The plugin can&#010;determine whether each project execution is successful, and optionally can&#010;verify the output generated from a given project execution.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-invoker-plugin/&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-invoker-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;1.9&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Invoker Plugin - Version 1.9&#010;&#010;Bugs:&#010;&#010; * [MINVOKER-162] - IT failure with empty local it-repo&#010; * [MINVOKER-166] - Failing in relationship with Maven 3.2.2&#010;&#010;Improvement:&#010;&#010; * [MINVOKER-119] - Allow access to properties in pre- and postBuild scripts&#010;&#010;New Features:&#010;&#010; * [MINVOKER-122] - Import information into groovy scripts of the running Maven environment&#010; * [MINVOKER-141] - passing own properties to all scripts&#010; * [MINVOKER-151] - Add failIfNoProjects&#010;&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Tue, 01 Jul 2014 19:51:51 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the Apache Doxia &#010;base and Doxia Site Tools 1.6, version 1.6&#010;&#010;Doxia is a content generation framework that provides powerful techniques for &#010;generating static and dynamic content, supporting a variety of markup &#010;languages.&#010;Doxia Site Tools is an extension of base Doxia component that generates either &#010;sites, consisting of decoration and content that was generated by Doxia, or &#010;documents like RTF or PDF.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/doxia/doxia/&#010;http://maven.apache.org/doxia/doxia-sitetools/&#010;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Doxia base - Version 1.6&#010;&#010;** Bug&#010;    * [DOXIA-386] - Snippet Macro:  Reference file does not support UTF-8 file &#010;format to generate the page garbage&#010;    * [DOXIA-503] - Plexus components cannot be abstract classes&#010;    * [DOXIA-509] - Multi-markdown metadata is too greedy&#010;    * [DOXIA-515] - &lt;div&gt; elements in markdown html block content are silently &#010;swallowed &#010;&#010;** Improvement&#010;    * [DOXIA-510] - create parser.module equivalent to module.site&#010;&#010;** Task&#010;    * [DOXIA-514] - Prepare unittests for JDK8&#010;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Doxia Sitetools - Version 1.6&#010;&#010;** Bug&#010;    * [DOXIASITETOOLS-76] - Missing inheritance of 'googleAdSenseClient', &#010;'googleAdSenseSlot' and 'googleAnalyticsAccountId' elements.&#010;    * [DOXIASITETOOLS-87] - inconsistent newlines between template content &#010;from skin and generated content&#010;    * [DOXIASITETOOLS-91] - Section title anchors are not at a good place in &#010;generated HTML&#010;&#010;** Improvement&#010;    * [DOXIASITETOOLS-84] - move o.a.m.doxia.sink.render.RenderingContext from &#010;Doxia core to Doxia Site Renderer&#010;    * [DOXIASITETOOLS-85] - move RenderingContext from o.a.m.doxia.sink.render &#010;package to o.a.m.doxia.siterenderer&#010;    * [DOXIASITETOOLS-86] - Use a linguisticly proper separator between &#010;project name and doc title in HTML title&#010;&#010;** New Feature&#010;    * [DOXIASITETOOLS-90] - site inheritance controllable&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010; Re: Running maven shade on a preexisting jar  
Date  :-

contents:- 
hi shade can possibly juxtapose jar deps diffrently from one build to the&#010;next in my experience. if you think you are having collisions you should&#010;probably do 2 things&#010;&#010;1) use &lt;exclude&gt; on the older jar from the older &lt;dependency&gt; to avoid the&#010;collision&#010;2) see if proguard fixes what shade breaks, if shade stays broken after #1.&#010; it's pretty intense&#010;&#010;&#010;On Mon, Jul 7, 2014 at 12:21 PM, Robert James &lt;srobertjames@gmail.com&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I have a jar that I need to shade - that is, change the name of many&#010;&gt; of the internal classes (to avoid conflicts with another jar) except&#010;&gt; for a few classes which remain exposed. Name  :- 
james northrup &lt;northrup.ja...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Running maven shade on a preexisting jar  
Date  :-
Mon, 07 Jul 2014 21:31:31 GMT  
contents:- 
shade is a uber jar plugin.  there are 3 uber jar plugins that matter,&#010;shade, maven-assembly, and proguard.&#010;&#010;for beginners:&#010;all of them work more or less by merging a project into a  single new jar&#010;just reading the pom dependencies.&#010;&#010;maven assembly does the least work.  good for quick jobs&#010;&#010;shade-plugin sometimes does a good job but imho if it works once you are&#010;buying into a false sense of security and will be bitten as you grow a&#010;project.&#010;&#010;proguard is industrial strength and imho returns the best result for&#010;investing in rtfm.&#010;&#010;all of the above have a special configs to do parts and pieces.  a&#010;beginner's mistake would be to pursue that course of action.  don't.  make&#010;a simple uber-jar project with one output jar combined from all of the&#010;input jars, and learn how to exclude collisions.&#010;&#010;if you have  some proprietary jar with no source spend some time with jad&#010;to make source and refactor your packages to do the above, "simple"&#010;uber-jar&#010;&#010;&#010;On Mon, Jul 7, 2014 at 2:15 PM, Robert James &lt;srobertjames@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; How do I run Maven Shade on a standalone jar (ie with no sources to&#010;&gt; build from)? Please realize that I'm a beginner to Maven.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 7/7/14, james northrup &lt;northrup.james@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt; hi shade can possibly juxtapose jar deps diffrently from one build to the&#010;&gt; &gt; next in my experience. if you think you are having collisions you should&#010;&gt; &gt; probably do 2 things&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; 1) use &lt;exclude&gt; on the older jar from the older &lt;dependency&gt; to avoid&#010;&gt; the&#010;&gt; &gt; collision&#010;&gt; &gt; 2) see if proguard fixes what shade breaks, if shade stays broken after&#010;&gt; #1.&#010;&gt; &gt;  it's pretty intense&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; On Mon, Jul 7, 2014 at 12:21 PM, Robert James &lt;srobertjames@gmail.com&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; I have a jar that I need to shade - that is, change the name of many&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; of the internal classes (to avoid conflicts with another jar) except&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; for a few classes which remain exposed.  The jar is already built,&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; source is not at hand.  How can I use maven shade to shade that jar?&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; (Disclaimer: I'm a maven neophyte)&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; --&#010;&gt; &gt; Jim Northrup  *  (408) 837-2270 *&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Jim Northrup  *  (408) 837-2270 *&#010;&#010;

Adding Classifiers when building  
Date  :-
Tue, 08 Jul 2014 08:21:41 GMT  
contents:- 
Hello Everyone&#010;&#010;I would like to know if it is possible to add classifiers while building as a maven parameter,&#010;for example if I want to add the classifier "dev" to an artifact, when building.&#010;&#010;Thank you in Advance, hope to hear from you.&#010;&#010;Best Regards&#010;Ruben Fragoso&#010;&#010;&#010;  

================

Name  :- 
Stephen Connolly &lt;stephen.alan.conno...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Adding Classifiers when building  
Date  :-
Tue, 08 Jul 2014 08:35:58 GMT  
contents:- 
Classifiers are not for what you think they are for... they are for&#010;flagging side artifacts... and in general they should not be used. A good&#010;example of a case for side artifacts is the javadocs.jar. You normally do&#010;not depend on the javadocs jar, it is a side artifact for IDEs.&#010;&#010;If you want to flag that a specific build is, e.g. for development use,&#010;then just reflect that in the version, i.e. 1.0-dev-1-SNAPSHOT&#010;&#010;&#010;On 8 July 2014 09:21, Fragoso, Ruben &lt;Ruben.Fragoso@ca.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hello Everyone&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I would like to know if it is possible to add classifiers while building&#010;&gt; as a maven parameter, for example if I want to add the classifier "dev" to&#010;&gt; an artifact, when building.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thank you in Advance, hope to hear from you.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Best Regards&#010;&gt; Ruben Fragoso&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;  

================

Name  :- 
Jason van Zyl &lt;ja...@takari.io&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Adding Classifiers when building  
Date  :-
Tue, 08 Jul 2014 12:47:37 GMT  
contents:- 
This is a bad practice and runs counter to continuous delivery which is commonly accepted as&#010;a good thing.&#010;&#010;You always want to build in such a way that anything being built can be used as a release&#010;without any further transformation.&#010;&#010;On Jul 8, 2014, at 4:21 AM, Fragoso, Ruben &lt;Ruben.Fragoso@ca.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hello Everyone&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I would like to know if it is possible to add classifiers while building as a maven parameter,&#010;for example if I want to add the classifier "dev" to an artifact, when building.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Thank you in Advance, hope to hear from you.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Best Regards&#010;&gt; Ruben Fragoso&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;&#010;Jason&#010;&#010;----------------------------------------------------------&#010;Jason van Zyl&#010;Founder,  Apache Maven&#010;http://twitter.com/jvanzyl&#010;http://twitter.com/takari_io&#010;---------------------------------------------------------&#010;&#010;I never make the mistake of arguing with people for whose opinions I have no respect.&#010;&#010;-- Edward Gibbon&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Stephen Connolly &lt;stephen.alan.conno...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Remote repositories protocols  
Date  :-
Wed, 09 Jul 2014 07:48:20 GMT  
contents:- 
wagon is the extension point to implement additional protocols. You need to&#010;register wagon implementations as extensions in order to use them in your&#010;pom (or register them as additional dependencies of specific plugins in&#010;your pom to use them for a specific plugin)&#010;&#010;&#010;On 9 July 2014 07:42, Eric Cornely &lt;ericcornely@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I read in the documentation (&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; https://maven.apache.org/guides/introduction/introduction-to-repositories.html&#010;&gt; )&#010;&gt; that "maven repositories can be accessed by a variety of protocols such as&#010;&gt; file:// and http://"&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; By curiosity I'm wondering what are the other protocols supported by maven.&#010;&gt; Is there a list of them or a way I could make it ? by listing existing&#010;&gt; wagon ? (Is wagon used only when deploy ?)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I'm really wondering about ftp://, ftps://, ssh://, sftp:// and smb://&#010;&gt; support. If you know one of these works as a repository url, tell me.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Kind regards,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Eric Cornely&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; Eric Cornely&#010;&gt; ericcornely@gmail.com&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Please consider the environment before printing this e-mail&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

If you know one of these works as a repository url, tell me.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Kind regards,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Eric Cornely&#010;&gt;&gt; --&#010;&gt;&gt; Eric Cornely&#010;&gt;&gt; ericcornely@gmail.com&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Please consider the environment before printing this e-mail&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

I did a google search for the answer. This says Eclipse defers to Oracle's&#010;javadoc.exe tool:&#010;http://help.eclipse.org/juno/index.jsp?topic=%2Forg.eclipse.jdt.doc.user%2Freference%2Fref-export-javadoc.htm&#010;&#010;So Eclipse must be configuring the tool in a way that doesn't trigger the&#010;NPE. Hi Russ,&#010;&#010;this can only be done programmatically in a plugin/MOJO.&#010;However, it is very easy: You need to invoke setFile(File) on the &#010;MavenProject:&#010;             this.project.setFile( flattenedPomFile );&#010;&#010;Before I also tried to configure maven-install-plugin and &#010;maven-deploy-plugin to use a different file, but these features have &#010;been removed in the recent versions. Also you would get trouble with &#010;further related plugins such as maven-gpg-plugin.&#010;&#010;Both ways are rather a workaround than a solid and well-designed solution.&#010;E.g. see last comment of this issue:&#010;http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MOJO-2030&#010;&#010;Start a discussion on the maven dev list if you like to. I think maven &#010;needs some re-design here...&#010;Also the way aggregators work has design issues. But chaning the maven &#010;plugin eco-system is quite of a challange. Maybe in maven 4 one day...&#010;&#010; &gt; Since your 99% there, maybe you could add a parameter to just let me &#010;add my own custom pom?&#010; &gt; Or can I just overwrite .flattened-pom.xml with my own?&#010;&#010;Would be easy to do. You can also overwrite the generated file but you &#010;have to be in the lifecycle after flatten plugin and right before any &#010;other plugin such as gpg or install.&#010;&#010;&gt; I find it is sometimes hard to get "non-religious" answers on the maven forums.  ;)&#010;&#010;Some time ago I had the same problem. Try to change the way you talk &#010;already helped for me :)&#010;Describe your problem precisely and then ask open questions. Remove all &#010;complaints before you hit "send" ;)&#010;&#010;Regards&#010;   Jörg&#010;&#010;Am 10.07.2014 04:14, schrieb Russ Tremain:&#010;&gt; Hi Jörg,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I'm giving your plugin a spin and I think it really helps!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; What I wonder is how do you get maven-install and maven-deploy plugins to use ${basedir}/.flattened-pom.xml&#010;?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Is there a magic property I can set, or can this only be done programatically? [ANN] Apache Maven Source Plugin 2.3 Released  
Date  :-
Fri, 11 Jul 2014 17:25:30 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the &#010;Apache Maven Source Plugin, version 2.3.&#010;&#010;The Source Plugin creates a jar archive of the source files of the current&#010;project. The jar file is, by default, created in the project's target&#010;directory.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-source-plugin/&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-source-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;2.3&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Source Plugin - Version 2.3&#010;&#010;&#010;Bugs:&#010;&#010; * [MSOURCES-63] - Non-working links on doc site&#010; * [MSOURCES-64] - forceCreation=true doesn't create test source package when src/test missing&#010;&#010;Improvements:&#010;&#010; * [MSOURCES-68] - Add Maven version used to Created-By entry in manifest&#010; * [MSOURCES-69] - Update version of plexus-archiver to 2.4.4&#010; * [MSOURCES-70] - Update of maven-invoker-plugin to 1.9&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Sat, 12 Jul 2014 15:41:14 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the Apache Maven &#010;Site Plugin, version 3.4&#010;&#010;The Site Plugin is used to generate a site for the project. The generated site &#010;also includes the project's reports that were configured in the POM.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-site-plugin/&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-site-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;3.4&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Site Plugin - Version 3.4&#010;&#010;** Bug&#010;    * [MSITE-121] - Generated html files contain inconsistent new lines&#010;    * [MSITE-665] - Site plugin version 3.2 seems to modify a project's &#010;classpath.&#010;    * [MSITE-716] - update doxia-integration-tools to 1.6&#010;    * [MSITE-718] - upgrade Doxia base to 1.6&#010;    * [MSITE-719] - upgrade Doxia Site Tools to 1.6&#010;&#010;** Improvement&#010;    * [MSITE-454] - Don't use aggregator mojos for default report set&#010;    * [MSITE-516] - reportPlugins should/could inherit more information from &#010;pluginManagement&#010;    * [MSITE-711] - add report's goal name to output&#010;    * [MSITE-713] - improve "Error during page generation" error message&#010;    * [MSITE-714] - display statistics about Doxia documents rendered&#010;    * [MSITE-720] - upgrade maven-reporting-exec to 1.2&#010;    * [MSITE-722] - align display info on executed reports&#010;&#010;** Task&#010;    * [MSITE-715] - refactor: split Mojos in sub-packages&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

[Announce] Release of SonarQube Maven Plugin 2.4  
Date  :-
Tue, 15 Jul 2014 15:08:12 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team is pleased to announce the release of the SonarQube Maven Plugin version 2.4.&#010;&#010;&#010;This plugin aims at running SonarQube analysis for Maven projects.&#010;&#010;http://mojo.codehaus.org/sonar-maven-plugin/index.html&#010;&#010;To get this update, simply specify the version in your project's plugin configuration: &#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;        &lt;groupId&gt;org.codehaus.mojo&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;        &lt;artifactId&gt;sonar-maven-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;        &lt;version&gt;2.4&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes&#010;&#010;    * [MSONAR-70] - Use every available "sonar.*" property when running an analysis with&#010;Maven&#010;    * [MSONAR-75] - Remove unexisting entries from "sonar.sources" and "sonar.tests" on&#010;projects with packaging=pom&#010;    * [MSONAR-81] - On "war" modules the directory containing the web resources ("src/main/webapp"&#010;by default) should be automatically added to "sonar.sources" &#010;    * [MSONAR-82] - By default the "pom.xml" file should be part of "sonar.sources" &#010;    * [MSONAR-83] - Populate sonar.libraries&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team.&#010;&#010;Julien HENRY &#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

[ANN] Release appassembler-maven-plugin Version 1.8.1 - Released  
Date  :-
Wed, 16 Jul 2014 17:37:25 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team is pleased to announce the release of the&#010;Appassembler Maven Plugin version 1.8.1.&#010;&#010;The Application Assembler Plugin is a Maven plugin for generating &#010;scripts for starting java applications. All dependencies and the &#010;artifact of the project itself are placed in a generated Maven &#010;repository in a defined assemble directory. All artifacts (dependencies &#010;+ the artifact from the project) are added to the classpath in the &#010;generated bin scripts.&#010;&#010;http://mojo.codehaus.org/appassembler/appassembler-maven-plugin/&#010;&#010;To get this update, simply specify the version in your project's plugin &#010;configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;   &lt;groupId&gt;org.codehaus.mojo&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;   &lt;artifactId&gt;appassembler-maven-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;   &lt;version&gt;1.8.1&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;Release Notes:&#010;http://jira.codehaus.org/secure/ReleaseNote.jspa?projectId=11780&amp;version=20322&#010;&#010;Bugs:&#010;&#010;  * [MAPPASM-121] - Generated script should be set executable (or allow &#010;for a umask to be defined).&#010;  * [MAPPASM-228] - [Daemon *nix template] Params of tr command must be &#010;quoted&#010;  * [MAPPASM-234] - Make unix scripts executable, but not &#010;world-writable, i.e. 0755 (on unix)&#010;&#010;Improvements:&#010;&#010;  * [MAPPASM-230] - Failed to create directory for log/temp files&#010;  * [MAPPASM-233] - Change integration tests according to &#010;maven-invoker-plugin 1.9 (mavenVersion) in verify.groovy&#010;&#010;Wish:&#010;&#010;  * [MAPPASM-54] - make unix scripts executable (on unix)&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team.&#010;&#010;Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi Alejandro,&#010;&#010;&gt; I have a java class that has a constant in it (static final String).&#010;&gt; This string is a version number, e.g. "1.3.2-test".&#010;&#010;Beware: the Java compiler often inlines constants, _including String&#010;constants_, into classes that reference the value. So if you compile a&#010;class "Foo" against version 1 of library "bar", then run with version 2 of&#010;"bar" in the classpath, Foo will still see the constant value as 1 instead&#010;of 2.&#010;&#010;http://javasplitter.blogspot.com/2011/10/static-final-inline-trap.html&#010;&#010;Much, much better to embed the version number into the JAR manifest, and/or&#010;read it out of the Maven POM which the maven-jar-plugin embeds in the JAR&#010;file.&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Curtis&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Jul 16, 2014 at 1:18 PM, &lt;Alejandro.Endo@miranda.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I have a java class that has a constant in it (static final String). This&#010;&gt; string is a version number, e.g. "1.3.2-test". I need to have this same&#010;&gt; value in a maven plugin configuration (the jaxb plugin) so I am wondering,&#010;&gt; is it better to keep the actual declaration in the code and somehow tell&#010;&gt; maven to take it from the code, or is it better to declare it in the pom&#010;&gt; and tell java to take the literal value to define the constant from the&#010;&gt; pom??&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I don't know how to do either so I would also like to hear some ideas. I&#010;&gt; am hoping i don't have to use resource filtering since having a source&#010;&gt; file as a resource is kind of problematic to me. It has to be ONLY that&#010;&gt; file that gets filtered, it would need to be in a non-standard location&#010;&gt; not src/main/java (maybe this is not true), and in general, it seems to me&#010;&gt; that treating source code as resource is counter-intuitive&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Has anyone else solved this issue with the DRY principle across behaviour&#010;&gt; and build system?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The short background is that maven generates an XML schema via jaxb and&#010;&gt; this schema file is then made available at runtime via a service&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thank you,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Alejandro Endo | Software Designer/Concepteur de logiciels&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; DISCLAIMER:&#010;&gt; Privileged and/or Confidential information may be contained in this&#010;&gt; message. If you are not the addressee of this message, you may not&#010;&gt; copy, use or deliver this message to anyone. In such event, you&#010;&gt; should destroy the message and kindly notify the sender by reply&#010;&gt; e-mail. Hi Alejandro,&#010;&#010;Alejandro.Endo@miranda.com wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi Curtis,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I *think* i see you point, but wouldn't that happen ONLY if the constant&#010;&gt; is public and referenced in a separate jar?? where it would be inlined in&#010;&gt; the referring class (right?). In my case the constant is package protected&#010;&gt; (it would be private if it wasn't because i need it in unit tests)&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; The problem with defining it in the manifest is that I use this constant&#010;&gt; in the property of an annotation of the class&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; @StaticServiceProperty(mandatory = true, type = "java.lang.String", name =&#010;&gt; "schemaVersion", value = SchemaProviderServiceImpl.SCHEMA_VERSION,&#010;&gt; immutable = true)&#010;&gt; public class SchemaProviderServiceImpl&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; so I can't grab it from the manifest at runtime. I guess the way I phrased&#010;&gt; it in the original email implied the opposite, sorry about that&#010;&#010;&#010;typical solution is to generate the source.&#010;&#010;Move the Java code that should contain the version into an own directory &#010;tree (e.g. src/main/java-templates). Replace the version string with an &#010;expression (e.g. "${project.version}") and use the copy-resources goal of &#010;the resources plugin to filter the file into a target driectory tree (e.g. &#010;target/generated-sources). Bind the goal to the generate-sources phase. Then &#010;use additionally the build-helper plugin to add target/generated-sources as &#010;additional source directory and you're done.&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;Jörg&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi,&#010;&#010; &gt; Move the Java code that should contain the version into an own directory&#010;&gt; tree (e.g. src/main/java-templates). Replace the version string with an&#010;&gt; expression (e.g. "${project.version}") and use the copy-resources goal of&#010;&gt; the resources plugin to filter the file into a target driectory tree (e.g.&#010;&gt; target/generated-sources). Bind the goal to the generate-sources phase. Then&#010;&gt; use additionally the build-helper plugin to add target/generated-sources as&#010;&gt; additional source directory and you're done.&#010;&#010;Best solution was already mentoined by Robert Scholte by using the &#010;templating-maven-plugin which exactly supports that scenario without &#010;supplemental addition of target/generated-sources folder by &#010;build-helpr-maven-plugin etc.&#010;&#010;Just simply create the template files in src/main/java-templates/ use &#010;the expressions etc. no need for supplemental configuration of &#010;maven-resources-plugin etc.&#010;&#010;Best and simple solution...which i wrote longer time a go a blog about&#010;http://blog.soebes.de/blog/2014/01/02/version-information-into-your-appas-with-maven/&#010;&#010;Kind regards&#010;Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi all,&#010;&#010;&gt; Best and simple solution...which i wrote longer time a go a blog about&#010;&gt;&#010;http://blog.soebes.de/blog/2014/01/02/version-information-into-your-appas-with-maven/&#010;&#010;I agree with Karl: I think it is much nicer to use the maven-jar-plugin to&#010;add the version to the JAR manifest, and just read it out of there, using&#010;the options:&#010;&#010;  &lt;addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;&#010;  &lt;addDefaultSpecificationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultSpecificationEntries&gt;&#010;&#010;That's not to say that code generation with Maven isn't awesome though.&#010;Codehaus deserves major kudos for the buildhelper-maven-plugin, especially&#010;since it is supported by M2E as well!&#010;&#010;In one my projects, we combine this with the groovy-maven-plugin and Apache&#010;Velocity to auto-generate many classes from templates in a loop.&#010;https://github.com/imagej/imagej-ops/blob/master/pom.xml#L190-L231&#010;&#010;I considered improving the velocity-maven-plugin [1] to support this sort&#010;of thing (reusing the same template to generate a list of classes), but the&#010;groovy approach is easy and works just fine.&#010;&#010;Now we just need an official Maven page about how to do this, since AFAICT&#010;all the existing blog posts and SO questions don't explain it very clearly.&#010;&#010;Great stuff,&#010;Curtis&#010;&#010;[1] https://code.google.com/p/velocity-maven-plugin/&#010;&#010;&#010;On Thu, Jul 17, 2014 at 10:18 AM, Karl Heinz Marbaise &lt;khmarbaise@gmx.de&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Move the Java code that should contain the version into an own directory&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; tree (e.g. src/main/java-templates). Replace the version string with an&#010;&gt;&gt; expression (e.g. "${project.version}") and use the copy-resources goal of&#010;&gt;&gt; the resources plugin to filter the file into a target driectory tree (e.g.&#010;&gt;&gt; target/generated-sources). Bind the goal to the generate-sources phase.&#010;&gt;&gt; Then&#010;&gt;&gt; use additionally the build-helper plugin to add target/generated-sources&#010;&gt;&gt; as&#010;&gt;&gt; additional source directory and you're done.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Best solution was already mentoined by Robert Scholte by using the&#010;&gt; templating-maven-plugin which exactly supports that scenario without&#010;&gt; supplemental addition of target/generated-sources folder by&#010;&gt; build-helpr-maven-plugin etc.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Just simply create the template files in src/main/java-templates/ use the&#010;&gt; expressions etc. no need for supplemental configuration of&#010;&gt; maven-resources-plugin etc.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Best and simple solution...which i wrote longer time a go a blog about&#010;&gt; http://blog.soebes.de/blog/2014/01/02/version-information-into-your-appas-&#010;&gt; with-maven/&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Kind regards&#010;&gt; Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

&gt; &gt; Best and simple solution...which i wrote longer time a go a blog about&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; http://blog.soebes.de/blog/2014/01/02/version-information-into-your-appas-with-maven/&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I agree with Karl: I think it is much nicer to use the maven-jar-plugin to&#010;&gt; add the version to the JAR manifest, and just read it out of there, using&#010;&gt; the options:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &lt;addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;&#010;&gt;   &lt;addDefaultSpecificationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultSpecificationEntries&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;There is one major drawback with using the manifest file. It will not work&#010;with unit tests as the manifest file isn't created until the jar is&#010;created. But if your unit tests don't touch any of the code that reads the&#010;manifest info that's not a problem.&#010;&#010;/Anders&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; That's not to say that code generation with Maven isn't awesome though.&#010;&gt; Codehaus deserves major kudos for the buildhelper-maven-plugin, especially&#010;&gt; since it is supported by M2E as well!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; In one my projects, we combine this with the groovy-maven-plugin and Apache&#010;&gt; Velocity to auto-generate many classes from templates in a loop.&#010;&gt; https://github.com/imagej/imagej-ops/blob/master/pom.xml#L190-L231&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I considered improving the velocity-maven-plugin [1] to support this sort&#010;&gt; of thing (reusing the same template to generate a list of classes), but the&#010;&gt; groovy approach is easy and works just fine.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Now we just need an official Maven page about how to do this, since AFAICT&#010;&gt; all the existing blog posts and SO questions don't explain it very clearly.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Great stuff,&#010;&gt; Curtis&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [1] https://code.google.com/p/velocity-maven-plugin/&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Thu, Jul 17, 2014 at 10:18 AM, Karl Heinz Marbaise &lt;khmarbaise@gmx.de&gt;&#010;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; Move the Java code that should contain the version into an own&#010;&gt; directory&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; tree (e.g. src/main/java-templates). Replace the version string with an&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; expression (e.g. "${project.version}") and use the copy-resources goal&#010;&gt; of&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; the resources plugin to filter the file into a target driectory tree&#010;&gt; (e.g.&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; target/generated-sources). Bind the goal to the generate-sources phase.&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; Then&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; use additionally the build-helper plugin to add target/generated-sources&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; as&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; additional source directory and you're done.&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Best solution was already mentoined by Robert Scholte by using the&#010;&gt; &gt; templating-maven-plugin which exactly supports that scenario without&#010;&gt; &gt; supplemental addition of target/generated-sources folder by&#010;&gt; &gt; build-helpr-maven-plugin etc.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Just simply create the template files in src/main/java-templates/ use the&#010;&gt; &gt; expressions etc. no need for supplemental configuration of&#010;&gt; &gt; maven-resources-plugin etc.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Best and simple solution...which i wrote longer time a go a blog about&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; http://blog.soebes.de/blog/2014/01/02/version-information-into-your-appas-&#010;&gt; &gt; with-maven/&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Kind regards&#010;&gt; &gt; Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; &gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

http://blog.soebes.de/blog/2014/01/02/version-information-into-your-appas-with-maven/&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I agree with Karl: I think it is much nicer to use the maven-jar-plugin to&#010;&gt; add the version to the JAR manifest, and just read it out of there, using&#010;&gt; the options:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;    &lt;addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;&#010;&gt;    &lt;addDefaultSpecificationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultSpecificationEntries&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; That's not to say that code generation with Maven isn't awesome though.&#010;&gt; Codehaus deserves major kudos for the buildhelper-maven-plugin, especially&#010;&gt; since it is supported by M2E as well!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Move the Java code that should contain the version into an own directory&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; tree (e.g. src/main/java-templates). Replace the version string with an&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; expression (e.g. "${project.version}") and use the copy-resources goal of&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; the resources plugin to filter the file into a target driectory tree (e.g.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; target/generated-sources). Bind the goal to the generate-sources phase.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Then&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; use additionally the build-helper plugin to add target/generated-sources&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; as&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; additional source directory and you're done.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Best solution was already mentoined by Robert Scholte by using the&#010;&gt;&gt; templating-maven-plugin which exactly supports that scenario without&#010;&gt;&gt; supplemental addition of target/generated-sources folder by&#010;&gt;&gt; build-helpr-maven-plugin etc.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Just simply create the template files in src/main/java-templates/ use the&#010;&gt;&gt; expressions etc. no need for supplemental configuration of&#010;&gt;&gt; maven-resources-plugin etc.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Best and simple solution...which i wrote longer time a go a blog about&#010;&gt;&gt; http://blog.soebes.de/blog/2014/01/02/version-information-into-your-appas-&#010;&gt;&gt; with-maven/&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Kind regards&#010;&gt;&gt; Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Ron Wheeler&#010;President&#010;Artifact Software Inc&#010;email: rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;skype: ronaldmwheeler&#010;phone: 866-970-2435, ext 102&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi Karl-Heinz,&#010;&#010;Karl Heinz Marbaise wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;  &gt; Move the Java code that should contain the version into an own&#010;&gt;  &gt; directory&#010;&gt;&gt; tree (e.g. src/main/java-templates). Replace the version string with an&#010;&gt;&gt; expression (e.g. "${project.version}") and use the copy-resources goal of&#010;&gt;&gt; the resources plugin to filter the file into a target driectory tree&#010;&gt;&gt; (e.g. target/generated-sources). Bind the goal to the generate-sources&#010;&gt;&gt; phase. Then use additionally the build-helper plugin to add&#010;&gt;&gt; target/generated-sources as additional source directory and you're done.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Best solution was already mentoined by Robert Scholte by using the&#010;&gt; templating-maven-plugin which exactly supports that scenario without&#010;&gt; supplemental addition of target/generated-sources folder by&#010;&gt; build-helpr-maven-plugin etc.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Just simply create the template files in src/main/java-templates/ use&#010;&gt; the expressions etc. no need for supplemental configuration of&#010;&gt; maven-resources-plugin etc.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Best and simple solution...which i wrote longer time a go a blog about&#010;&gt; http://blog.soebes.de/blog/2014/01/02/version-information-into-your-appas-with-maven/&#010;&#010;nice article ;-)&#010;&#010;There's one comment I do not understand though:&#010;&#010;&gt; The main disadvantage of this approach is that you can only use the&#010;&gt; Implementation and Specification parts of your MANIFEST.MF file which&#010;&gt; might be enough in some situations but not in all.&#010;&#010;You can add all kind of entries to the manifest. You may even overwrite the &#010;defaults. We use typically:&#010;&#010;===================== %&lt; ======================&#010; &lt;archive&gt;&#010;   &lt;manifest&gt;&#010;     &lt;addDefaultSpecificationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultSpecificationEntries&gt;&#010;     &lt;addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;&#010;   &lt;/manifest&gt;&#009;&#009;&#009;&#009;&#009;&#009;&#010;   &lt;manifestEntries&gt;&#010;     &lt;Specification-Version&gt;${parsedVersion.majorVersion}.&#010;${parsedVersion.minorVersion}&lt;/Specification-Version&gt;&#010;     &lt;X-Compile-Source&gt;${java.version.source}&lt;/X-Compile-Source&gt;&#010;     &lt;X-Compile-Target&gt;${java.version.target}&lt;/X-Compile-Target&gt;&#010;     &lt;X-Builder&gt;Maven ${maven.version}&lt;/X-Builder&gt;&#010;     &lt;X-Build-Time&gt;${maven.build.timestamp}&lt;/X-Build-Time&gt;&#010;     &lt;X-Build-Os&gt;${os.name}&lt;/X-Build-Os&gt;&#010;   &lt;/manifestEntries&gt;&#010; &lt;/archive&gt;&#010;===================== %&lt; ======================&#010;&#010;With the $parsedVersion and $maven.version variables provided by the build-&#010;helper plugin.&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;Jörg&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi Jörg,&#010;&#010; &gt;&#010;&gt; nice article ;-)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; There's one comment I do not understand though:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The main disadvantage of this approach is that you can only use the&#010;&gt;&gt; Implementation and Specification parts of your MANIFEST.MF file which&#010;&gt;&gt; might be enough in some situations but not in all.&#010;&#010;The comment is related to the implementation in Java which allows only &#010;to extract the implementation and specification part...via&#010;this.getClass().getPackage()....&#010;&#010;http://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/api/java/lang/Package.html&#010;So can't use that in a very simple way...&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; You can add all kind of entries to the manifest. You may even overwrite the&#010;&gt; defaults. We use typically:&#010;&#010;Of course you can so create an appropriate MANIFEST.MF file...&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ===================== %&lt; ======================&#010;&gt;   &lt;archive&gt;&#010;&gt;     &lt;manifest&gt;&#010;&gt;       &lt;addDefaultSpecificationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultSpecificationEntries&gt;&#010;&gt;       &lt;addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;&#010;&gt;     &lt;/manifest&gt;&#009;&#009;&#009;&#009;&#009;&#009;&#010;&gt;     &lt;manifestEntries&gt;&#010;&gt;       &lt;Specification-Version&gt;${parsedVersion.majorVersion}.&#010;&gt; ${parsedVersion.minorVersion}&lt;/Specification-Version&gt;&#010;&gt;       &lt;X-Compile-Source&gt;${java.version.source}&lt;/X-Compile-Source&gt;&#010;&gt;       &lt;X-Compile-Target&gt;${java.version.target}&lt;/X-Compile-Target&gt;&#010;&gt;       &lt;X-Builder&gt;Maven ${maven.version}&lt;/X-Builder&gt;&#010;&gt;       &lt;X-Build-Time&gt;${maven.build.timestamp}&lt;/X-Build-Time&gt;&#010;&gt;       &lt;X-Build-Os&gt;${os.name}&lt;/X-Build-Os&gt;&#010;&gt;     &lt;/manifestEntries&gt;&#010;&gt;   &lt;/archive&gt;&#010;&gt; ===================== %&lt; ======================&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; With the $parsedVersion and $maven.version variables provided by the build-&#010;&gt; helper plugin.&#010;But the above entries can't be read via methods which already exists &#010;like getPackage()....&#010;&#010;So you need to implement it your own...you have to take care about &#010;classloading issue (classloaders in particular in larger apps etc.)...&#010;so it get more and more complicated...lets talk about apps which &#010;comprise of 150 jar files...&#010;&#010;So the simplest Solution is to use the templating-maven-plugin which &#010;solves many of those issues.&#010;&#010;Kind regards&#010;Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010; There is a very simple process here. Turn on filtering in the resource&#010;plugin, and add a .properties file that filters in what you need. Then&#010;get those properties. No problems with unit tests, no problems keeping&#010;track of _which_ MANIFEST.MF from classpath is the one you need.&#010;&#010;On Fri, Jul 18, 2014 at 4:33 PM, Karl Heinz Marbaise &lt;khmarbaise@gmx.de&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; Hi Jörg,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; nice article ;-)&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; There's one comment I do not understand though:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; The main disadvantage of this approach is that you can only use the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Implementation and Specification parts of your MANIFEST.MF file which&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; might be enough in some situations but not in all.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The comment is related to the implementation in Java which allows only to&#010;&gt; extract the implementation and specification part...via&#010;&gt; this.getClass().getPackage()....&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; http://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/api/java/lang/Package.html&#010;&gt; So can't use that in a very simple way...&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; You can add all kind of entries to the manifest. You may even overwrite&#010;&gt;&gt; the&#010;&gt;&gt; defaults. We use typically:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Of course you can so create an appropriate MANIFEST.MF file...&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; ===================== %&lt; ======================&#010;&gt;&gt;   &lt;archive&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;manifest&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;addDefaultSpecificationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultSpecificationEntries&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;/manifest&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;manifestEntries&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;Specification-Version&gt;${parsedVersion.majorVersion}.&#010;&gt;&gt; ${parsedVersion.minorVersion}&lt;/Specification-Version&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;X-Compile-Source&gt;${java.version.source}&lt;/X-Compile-Source&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;X-Compile-Target&gt;${java.version.target}&lt;/X-Compile-Target&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;X-Builder&gt;Maven ${maven.version}&lt;/X-Builder&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;X-Build-Time&gt;${maven.build.timestamp}&lt;/X-Build-Time&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;X-Build-Os&gt;${os.name}&lt;/X-Build-Os&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;/manifestEntries&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;   &lt;/archive&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; ===================== %&lt; ======================&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; With the $parsedVersion and $maven.version variables provided by the&#010;&gt;&gt; build-&#010;&gt;&gt; helper plugin.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; But the above entries can't be read via methods which already exists like&#010;&gt; getPackage()....&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So you need to implement it your own...you have to take care about&#010;&gt; classloading issue (classloaders in particular in larger apps etc.)...&#010;&gt; so it get more and more complicated...lets talk about apps which comprise of&#010;&gt; 150 jar files...&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So the simplest Solution is to use the templating-maven-plugin which solves&#010;&gt; many of those issues.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Kind regards&#010;&gt; Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; Subject  :-
Welcome our new VP of Apache Maven, Hervé Boutemy  
Date  :-
Sat, 19 Jul 2014 21:42:16 GMT  
contents:- 
The role of VP of maven is more a technical and legal responsibility in&#010;that the ASF board requires an officer of the foundation to delegate the&#010;powers vested in the PMC to.&#010;&#010;A few years back, John Casey suggested that we should try rotating this&#010;burden amongst the PMC on a yearly-ish basis.&#010;&#010;I have been PMC chair for the last year, and it has been fun times, but&#010;when I took the unlucky victim role I said it would be for one year only.&#010;&#010;True to my word, I asked the PMC to nominate a replacement. Hervé was&#010;selected and at the most recent board meeting I was released from these&#010;responsibilities with board approving Hervé as our new VP&#010;&#010;Everyone please congratulate Hervé on being our next unlucky victim!&#010;&#010;Please also remember that it is the community that determines the direction&#010;of this project. The PMC is there to ensure the project plays by the rules,&#010;the PMC chair is here to serve the project, board and PMC.&#010;&#010;I wish Hervé all the best for his stint... And I won't fear taking the&#010;baton up again next time ;-)&#010;&#010;- Stephen&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Sent from my phone&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Olivier Lamy &lt;ol...@apache.org&gt;  
Subject  :-
[ANN] Apache Archiva 2.1.0  
Date  :-
Sun, 20 Jul 2014 03:28:16 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;The Apache Archiva team would like to announce the release of Archiva&#010;2.1.0. Archiva is available for download from the web site (&#010;http://archiva.apache.org )&#010;&#010;Archiva is an application for managing one or more remote&#010;repositories, including administration, artifact handling, browsing&#010;and searching.&#010;&#010;If you have any questions, please consult:&#010;&#010;the web site: http://archiva.apache.org/&#010;the archiva-user mailing list: http://archiva.apache.org/mail-lists.html&#010;&#010;New in Archiva 2.1.0&#010;&#010;Apache Archiva 2.1.0 is a bugs fix release:&#010;&#010;NOTE: jdk 1.7 is now prerequisite with Apache Archiva 1.7&#010;&#010;Compatibility Changes&#010;&#010;If upgrading from earlier versions of Archiva, the list of libraries&#010;in wrapper.conf has changed. If you have customized your copy of&#010;wrapper.conf, please update it for compatibility with the version&#010;distributed with the current release.&#010;As the database storage has been removed, you can remove the JNDI&#010;entry for jdbc/archiva. After upgrading from a previous version, you&#010;will have to run a full scan to populate the new JCR Repository. This&#010;will be done on first start of Archiva.&#010;&#010;Refer to the Upgrading Archiva guide for more information.&#010;&#010;Release Notes&#010;&#010;The Archiva 2.1.0 features set can be seen in the feature tour.&#010;&#010;Changes in Archiva 2.1.0&#010;&#010;Released: 20th July 2014&#010;&#010;Improvement&#010;&#010;[MRM-1210] - Dependency tree should include the artifact type&#010;[MRM-1558] - Please provide some UI element which shows degraded&#010;and/or badly connected remote repository&#010;[MRM-1802] - Find a cache solution for browsing part (especially root browsing)&#010;[MRM-1829] - Change default value of of AysncLogger strategy for log4j async&#010;[MRM-1834] - Add limit to index search query to prevent unnecessary calculations&#010;[MRM-1836] - Make search limit (maxCount) configurable via UI&#010;[MRM-1843] - provide mechanism to obtain the latest version of an artifact&#010;&#010;Bug&#010;&#010;[MRM-887] - Start script has no valid "uname" option&#010;[MRM-1809] - Users - Manage section sort by name doesn't work as expected&#010;[MRM-1812] - Users - Manage section needs Sort by User Name, Sort by&#010;Full Name, and Sort by Email buttons&#010;[MRM-1813] - Users - Manage section filters don't seem to work&#010;[MRM-1823] - java 1.7 as prerequisite&#010;[MRM-1824] - metadata storage using Cassandra&#010;[MRM-1825] - MD5 hashes are for wrong file name&#010;[MRM-1826] - Force Internet Explorer into Standards Mode&#010;[MRM-1830] - Charset applied to binary repository HTTP responses&#010;[MRM-1833] - Nullpointer when browsing artifacts which have&#010;dependencies with scope "import"&#010;[MRM-1837] - DefaultArchivaConfiguration holds references to classes&#010;[MRM-1841] - "Remember me" not working&#010;[MRM-1842] - Remove per default log4j2 Async Logging&#010;[MRM-1846] - Regression in 2.0.1 : uniqueVersion false not supported&#010;[MRM-1849] - Unable to download -SNAPSHOT jars after 2.0.1 Upgrade&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;Have fun!&#010;-- &#010;The Apache Archiva Team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Here is an aar straight from Axis version example:&#010;&#010;//layout of version.aar:&#010;&#010;   created: META-INF/&#010;  inflated: META-INF/MANIFEST.MF&#010;   created: sample/&#010;   created: sample/axisversion/&#010;  inflated: sample/axisversion/Version.class&#010;  inflated: META-INF/services.xml&#010;&#010;&#010;//org.apache.axis2.deployment.DeploymentEngine axis code used to populateService with .aar&#010;contents:&#010;&#010;    protected ArrayList populateService(AxisServiceGroup serviceGroup,&#010;                                        URL servicesURL,&#010;                                        String serviceName) throws DeploymentException {&#010;        try {&#010;            serviceGroup.setServiceGroupName(serviceName);&#010;            ClassLoader serviceClassLoader = Utils.createClassLoader(&#010;                    new URL[]{servicesURL},&#010;                    axisConfig.getServiceClassLoader(),&#010;                    true,&#010;                    (File) axisConfig.getParameterValue(Constants.Configuration.ARTIFACTS_TEMP_DIR),&#010;                    axisConfig.isChildFirstClassLoading());&#010;            String metainf = "meta-inf";&#010;            serviceGroup.setServiceGroupClassLoader(serviceClassLoader);&#010;            //processing wsdl.list&#010;            InputStream wsdlfilesStream =&#010;                    serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream("meta-inf/wsdl.list");&#010;            if (wsdlfilesStream == null) {&#010;                wsdlfilesStream = serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream("META-INF/wsdl.list");&#010;                if (wsdlfilesStream != null) {&#010;                    metainf = "META-INF";&#010;                }&#010;            }&#010;            HashMap servicesMap = new HashMap();&#010;            if (wsdlfilesStream != null) {&#010;                ArchiveReader reader = new ArchiveReader();&#010;                BufferedReader input = new BufferedReader(new InputStreamReader(wsdlfilesStream));&#010;                String line;&#010;                while ((line = input.readLine()) != null) {&#010;                    line = line.trim();&#010;                    if (line.length() &gt; 0 &amp;&amp; line.charAt(0) != '#') {&#010;                        line = metainf + "/" + line;&#010;                        try {&#010;                            List services = reader.getAxisServiceFromWsdl(&#010;                                    serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream(line),&#010;                                    serviceClassLoader, line);&#010;                            if (services != null) {&#010;                                for (Object service : services) {&#010;                                    AxisService axisService = (AxisService) service;&#010;                                    servicesMap.put(axisService.getName(), axisService);&#010;                                }&#010;                            }&#010;&#010;                        } catch (Exception e) {&#010;                            throw new DeploymentException(e);&#010;                        }&#010;                    }&#010;                }&#010;            }&#010;            InputStream servicexmlStream =&#010;                    serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream("META-INF/services.xml");&#010;            if (servicexmlStream == null) {&#010;                servicexmlStream = serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream("meta-inf/services.xml");&#010;            } else {&#010;                metainf = "META-INF";&#010;            }&#010;            if (servicexmlStream == null) {&#010;                throw new DeploymentException(&#010;                        Messages.getMessage(DeploymentErrorMsgs.SERVICE_XML_NOT_FOUND,&#010;                                servicesURL.toString()));&#010;            }&#010;            DescriptionBuilder builder = new DescriptionBuilder(servicexmlStream, configContext);&#010;            OMElement rootElement = builder.buildOM();&#010;            String elementName = rootElement.getLocalName();&#010;&#010;            if (TAG_SERVICE.equals(elementName)) {&#010;                AxisService axisService = null;&#010;                String wsdlLocation = "META-INF/service.wsdl";&#010;                InputStream wsdlStream =&#010;                        serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream(wsdlLocation);&#010;                URL wsdlURL = serviceClassLoader.getResource(metainf + "/service.wsdl");&#010;                if (wsdlStream == null) {&#010;                    wsdlLocation = "META-INF/" + serviceName + ".wsdl";&#010;                    wsdlStream = serviceClassLoader&#010;                            .getResourceAsStream(wsdlLocation);&#010;                    wsdlURL = serviceClassLoader.getResource(wsdlLocation);&#010;                }&#010;                if (wsdlStream != null) {&#010;                    WSDL11ToAxisServiceBuilder wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder =&#010;                            new WSDL11ToAxisServiceBuilder(wsdlStream, null, null);&#010;                    File file = Utils.toFile(servicesURL);&#010;                    if (file != null &amp;&amp; file.exists()) {&#010;                        wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.setCustomWSDLResolver(&#010;                                new AARBasedWSDLLocator(wsdlLocation, file, wsdlStream));&#010;                        wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.setCustomResolver(&#010;                                new AARFileBasedURIResolver(file));&#010;                    }&#010;                    if (wsdlURL != null) {&#010;                        wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.setDocumentBaseUri(wsdlURL.toString());&#010;                    }&#010;                    axisService = wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.populateService();&#010;                    axisService.setWsdlFound(true);&#010;                    axisService.setCustomWsdl(true);&#010;                    axisService.setName(serviceName);&#010;                }&#010;                if (axisService == null) {&#010;                    axisService = new AxisService(serviceName);&#010;                }&#010;&#010;                axisService.setParent(serviceGroup);&#010;                axisService.setClassLoader(serviceClassLoader);&#010;&#010;                ServiceBuilder serviceBuilder = new ServiceBuilder(configContext, axisService);&#010;                AxisService service = serviceBuilder.populateService(rootElement);&#010;&#010;                ArrayList serviceList = new ArrayList();&#010;                serviceList.add(service);&#010;                return serviceList;&#010;            } else if (TAG_SERVICE_GROUP.equals(elementName)) {&#010;                ServiceGroupBuilder groupBuilder = new ServiceGroupBuilder(rootElement, servicesMap,&#010;                        configContext);&#010;                ArrayList servicList = groupBuilder.populateServiceGroup(serviceGroup);&#010;                Iterator serviceIterator = servicList.iterator();&#010;                while (serviceIterator.hasNext()) {&#010;                    AxisService axisService = (AxisService) serviceIterator.next();&#010;                    String wsdlLocation = "META-INF/service.wsdl";&#010;                    InputStream wsdlStream =&#010;                            serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream(wsdlLocation);&#010;                    URL wsdlURL = serviceClassLoader.getResource(wsdlLocation);&#010;                    if (wsdlStream == null) {&#010;                        wsdlLocation = "META-INF/" + serviceName + ".wsdl";&#010;                        wsdlStream = serviceClassLoader&#010;                                .getResourceAsStream(wsdlLocation);&#010;                        wsdlURL =&#010;                                serviceClassLoader.getResource(wsdlLocation);&#010;                    }&#010;                    if (wsdlStream != null) {&#010;                        WSDL11ToAxisServiceBuilder wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder =&#010;                                new WSDL11ToAxisServiceBuilder(wsdlStream, axisService);&#010;                        File file = Utils.toFile(servicesURL);&#010;                        if (file != null &amp;&amp; file.exists()) {&#010;                            wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.setCustomWSDLResolver(&#010;                                    new AARBasedWSDLLocator(wsdlLocation, file, wsdlStream));&#010;                            wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.setCustomResolver(&#010;                                    new AARFileBasedURIResolver(file));&#010;                        }&#010;                        if (wsdlURL != null) {&#010;                            wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.setDocumentBaseUri(wsdlURL.toString());&#010;                        }&#010;                        axisService = wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.populateService();&#010;                        axisService.setWsdlFound(true);&#010;                        axisService.setCustomWsdl(true);&#010;                        // Set the default message receiver for the operations that were&#010;                        // not listed in the services.xml&#010;                        Iterator operations = axisService.getOperations();&#010;                        while (operations.hasNext()) {&#010;                            AxisOperation operation = (AxisOperation) operations.next();&#010;                            if (operation.getMessageReceiver() == null) {&#010;                                operation.setMessageReceiver(loadDefaultMessageReceiver(&#010;                                        operation.getMessageExchangePattern(), axisService));&#010;                            }&#010;                        }&#010;                    }&#010;                }&#010;                return servicList;&#010;            }&#010;        } catch (IOException e) {&#010;            throw new DeploymentException(e);&#010;        } catch (XMLStreamException e) {&#010;            throw new DeploymentException(e);&#010;        }&#010;        return null;&#010;    }&#010;&#010;does this answer your question?&#010;Martin &#010;______________&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; Date: Tue, 22 Jul 2014 07:56:55 +1000&#010;&gt; Subject: Re: maven-dependency-plugin unpacking aar format?&#010;&gt;
