No that was just an example so I could create a sample project.  Don't read&#010;too much into this.  They are just AAR dependencies (in my case they come&#010;from our build not public).  The maven dependency plugin should handle&#010;these no different than it handles jars/etc.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;On Mon, Jul 21, 2014 at 11:32 PM, William Ferguson &lt;&#010;william.ferguson@xandar.com.au&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; So an Android library is packaging WSDL inside itself and is expecting you&#010;&gt; to use it at build time?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Tue, Jul 22, 2014 at 8:53 AM, Martin Gainty &lt;mgainty@hotmail.com&gt;&#010;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Here is an aar straight from Axis version example:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; //layout of version.aar:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;    created: META-INF/&#010;&gt; &gt;   inflated: META-INF/MANIFEST.MF&#010;&gt; &gt;    created: sample/&#010;&gt; &gt;    created: sample/axisversion/&#010;&gt; &gt;   inflated: sample/axisversion/Version.class&#010;&gt; &gt;   inflated: META-INF/services.xml&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; //org.apache.axis2.deployment.DeploymentEngine axis code used to&#010;&gt; &gt; populateService with .aar contents:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;     protected ArrayList populateService(AxisServiceGroup serviceGroup,&#010;&gt; &gt;                                         URL servicesURL,&#010;&gt; &gt;                                         String serviceName) throws&#010;&gt; &gt; DeploymentException {&#010;&gt; &gt;         try {&#010;&gt; &gt;             serviceGroup.setServiceGroupName(serviceName);&#010;&gt; &gt;             ClassLoader serviceClassLoader = Utils.createClassLoader(&#010;&gt; &gt;                     new URL[]{servicesURL},&#010;&gt; &gt;                     axisConfig.getServiceClassLoader(),&#010;&gt; &gt;                     true,&#010;&gt; &gt;                     (File)&#010;&gt; &gt; axisConfig.getParameterValue(Constants.Configuration.ARTIFACTS_TEMP_DIR),&#010;&gt; &gt;                     axisConfig.isChildFirstClassLoading());&#010;&gt; &gt;             String metainf = "meta-inf";&#010;&gt; &gt;             serviceGroup.setServiceGroupClassLoader(serviceClassLoader);&#010;&gt; &gt;             //processing wsdl.list&#010;&gt; &gt;             InputStream wsdlfilesStream =&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream("meta-inf/wsdl.list");&#010;&gt; &gt;             if (wsdlfilesStream == null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                 wsdlfilesStream =&#010;&gt; &gt; serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream("META-INF/wsdl.list");&#010;&gt; &gt;                 if (wsdlfilesStream != null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                     metainf = "META-INF";&#010;&gt; &gt;                 }&#010;&gt; &gt;             }&#010;&gt; &gt;             HashMap servicesMap = new HashMap();&#010;&gt; &gt;             if (wsdlfilesStream != null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                 ArchiveReader reader = new ArchiveReader();&#010;&gt; &gt;                 BufferedReader input = new BufferedReader(new&#010;&gt; &gt; InputStreamReader(wsdlfilesStream));&#010;&gt; &gt;                 String line;&#010;&gt; &gt;                 while ((line = input.readLine()) != null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                     line = line.trim();&#010;&gt; &gt;                     if (line.length() &gt; 0 &amp;&amp; line.charAt(0) != '#') {&#010;&gt; &gt;                         line = metainf + "/" + line;&#010;&gt; &gt;                         try {&#010;&gt; &gt;                             List services =&#010;&gt; reader.getAxisServiceFromWsdl(&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream(line),&#010;&gt; &gt;                                     serviceClassLoader, line);&#010;&gt; &gt;                             if (services != null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                                 for (Object service : services) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                                     AxisService axisService =&#010;&gt; &gt; (AxisService) service;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; servicesMap.put(axisService.getName(),&#010;&gt; &gt; axisService);&#010;&gt; &gt;                                 }&#010;&gt; &gt;                             }&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;                         } catch (Exception e) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                             throw new DeploymentException(e);&#010;&gt; &gt;                         }&#010;&gt; &gt;                     }&#010;&gt; &gt;                 }&#010;&gt; &gt;             }&#010;&gt; &gt;             InputStream servicexmlStream =&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream("META-INF/services.xml");&#010;&gt; &gt;             if (servicexmlStream == null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                 servicexmlStream =&#010;&gt; &gt; serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream("meta-inf/services.xml");&#010;&gt; &gt;             } else {&#010;&gt; &gt;                 metainf = "META-INF";&#010;&gt; &gt;             }&#010;&gt; &gt;             if (servicexmlStream == null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                 throw new DeploymentException(&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Messages.getMessage(DeploymentErrorMsgs.SERVICE_XML_NOT_FOUND,&#010;&gt; &gt;                                 servicesURL.toString()));&#010;&gt; &gt;             }&#010;&gt; &gt;             DescriptionBuilder builder = new&#010;&gt; &gt; DescriptionBuilder(servicexmlStream, configContext);&#010;&gt; &gt;             OMElement rootElement = builder.buildOM();&#010;&gt; &gt;             String elementName = rootElement.getLocalName();&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;             if (TAG_SERVICE.equals(elementName)) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                 AxisService axisService = null;&#010;&gt; &gt;                 String wsdlLocation = "META-INF/service.wsdl";&#010;&gt; &gt;                 InputStream wsdlStream =&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream(wsdlLocation);&#010;&gt; &gt;                 URL wsdlURL = serviceClassLoader.getResource(metainf +&#010;&gt; &gt; "/service.wsdl");&#010;&gt; &gt;                 if (wsdlStream == null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                     wsdlLocation = "META-INF/" + serviceName + ".wsdl";&#010;&gt; &gt;                     wsdlStream = serviceClassLoader&#010;&gt; &gt;                             .getResourceAsStream(wsdlLocation);&#010;&gt; &gt;                     wsdlURL =&#010;&gt; serviceClassLoader.getResource(wsdlLocation);&#010;&gt; &gt;                 }&#010;&gt; &gt;                 if (wsdlStream != null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                     WSDL11ToAxisServiceBuilder wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder =&#010;&gt; &gt;                             new WSDL11ToAxisServiceBuilder(wsdlStream,&#010;&gt; &gt; null, null);&#010;&gt; &gt;                     File file = Utils.toFile(servicesURL);&#010;&gt; &gt;                     if (file != null &amp;&amp; file.exists()) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                         wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.setCustomWSDLResolver(&#010;&gt; &gt;                                 new AARBasedWSDLLocator(wsdlLocation,&#010;&gt; &gt; file, wsdlStream));&#010;&gt; &gt;                         wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.setCustomResolver(&#010;&gt; &gt;                                 new AARFileBasedURIResolver(file));&#010;&gt; &gt;                     }&#010;&gt; &gt;                     if (wsdlURL != null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.setDocumentBaseUri(wsdlURL.toString());&#010;&gt; &gt;                     }&#010;&gt; &gt;                     axisService =&#010;&gt; &gt; wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.populateService();&#010;&gt; &gt;                     axisService.setWsdlFound(true);&#010;&gt; &gt;                     axisService.setCustomWsdl(true);&#010;&gt; &gt;                     axisService.setName(serviceName);&#010;&gt; &gt;                 }&#010;&gt; &gt;                 if (axisService == null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                     axisService = new AxisService(serviceName);&#010;&gt; &gt;                 }&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;                 axisService.setParent(serviceGroup);&#010;&gt; &gt;                 axisService.setClassLoader(serviceClassLoader);&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;                 ServiceBuilder serviceBuilder = new&#010;&gt; &gt; ServiceBuilder(configContext, axisService);&#010;&gt; &gt;                 AxisService service =&#010;&gt; &gt; serviceBuilder.populateService(rootElement);&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;                 ArrayList serviceList = new ArrayList();&#010;&gt; &gt;                 serviceList.add(service);&#010;&gt; &gt;                 return serviceList;&#010;&gt; &gt;             } else if (TAG_SERVICE_GROUP.equals(elementName)) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                 ServiceGroupBuilder groupBuilder = new&#010;&gt; &gt; ServiceGroupBuilder(rootElement, servicesMap,&#010;&gt; &gt;                         configContext);&#010;&gt; &gt;                 ArrayList servicList =&#010;&gt; &gt; groupBuilder.populateServiceGroup(serviceGroup);&#010;&gt; &gt;                 Iterator serviceIterator = servicList.iterator();&#010;&gt; &gt;                 while (serviceIterator.hasNext()) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                     AxisService axisService = (AxisService)&#010;&gt; &gt; serviceIterator.next();&#010;&gt; &gt;                     String wsdlLocation = "META-INF/service.wsdl";&#010;&gt; &gt;                     InputStream wsdlStream =&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; serviceClassLoader.getResourceAsStream(wsdlLocation);&#010;&gt; &gt;                     URL wsdlURL =&#010;&gt; &gt; serviceClassLoader.getResource(wsdlLocation);&#010;&gt; &gt;                     if (wsdlStream == null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                         wsdlLocation = "META-INF/" + serviceName +&#010;&gt; ".wsdl";&#010;&gt; &gt;                         wsdlStream = serviceClassLoader&#010;&gt; &gt;                                 .getResourceAsStream(wsdlLocation);&#010;&gt; &gt;                         wsdlURL =&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; serviceClassLoader.getResource(wsdlLocation);&#010;&gt; &gt;                     }&#010;&gt; &gt;                     if (wsdlStream != null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                         WSDL11ToAxisServiceBuilder&#010;&gt; wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder&#010;&gt; &gt; =&#010;&gt; &gt;                                 new&#010;&gt; WSDL11ToAxisServiceBuilder(wsdlStream,&#010;&gt; &gt; axisService);&#010;&gt; &gt;                         File file = Utils.toFile(servicesURL);&#010;&gt; &gt;                         if (file != null &amp;&amp; file.exists()) {&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.setCustomWSDLResolver(&#010;&gt; &gt;                                     new AARBasedWSDLLocator(wsdlLocation,&#010;&gt; &gt; file, wsdlStream));&#010;&gt; &gt;                             wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.setCustomResolver(&#010;&gt; &gt;                                     new AARFileBasedURIResolver(file));&#010;&gt; &gt;                         }&#010;&gt; &gt;                         if (wsdlURL != null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.setDocumentBaseUri(wsdlURL.toString());&#010;&gt; &gt;                         }&#010;&gt; &gt;                         axisService =&#010;&gt; &gt; wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder.populateService();&#010;&gt; &gt;                         axisService.setWsdlFound(true);&#010;&gt; &gt;                         axisService.setCustomWsdl(true);&#010;&gt; &gt;                         // Set the default message receiver for the&#010;&gt; &gt; operations that were&#010;&gt; &gt;                         // not listed in the services.xml&#010;&gt; &gt;                         Iterator operations =&#010;&gt; axisService.getOperations();&#010;&gt; &gt;                         while (operations.hasNext()) {&#010;&gt; &gt;                             AxisOperation operation = (AxisOperation)&#010;&gt; &gt; operations.next();&#010;&gt; &gt;                             if (operation.getMessageReceiver() == null) {&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; operation.setMessageReceiver(loadDefaultMessageReceiver(&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; operation.getMessageExchangePattern(), axisService));&#010;&gt; &gt;                             }&#010;&gt; &gt;                         }&#010;&gt; &gt;                     }&#010;&gt; &gt;                 }&#010;&gt; &gt;                 return servicList;&#010;&gt; &gt;             }&#010;&gt; &gt;         } catch (IOException e) {&#010;&gt; &gt;             throw new DeploymentException(e);&#010;&gt; &gt;         } catch (XMLStreamException e) {&#010;&gt; &gt;             throw new DeploymentException(e);&#010;&gt; &gt;         }&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;                        // Set the default message receiver for the&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; operations that were&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;                        // not listed in the services.xml&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;                        Iterator operations =&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; axisService.getOperations();&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;                        while (operations.hasNext()) {&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;                            }&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;                        }&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;                    }&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;                }&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;                return servicList;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;            }&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;        } catch (IOException e) {&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;            throw new DeploymentException(e);&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;        } catch (XMLStreamException e) {&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;            throw new DeploymentException(e);&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;        }&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;        return null;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;                }&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;                if (wsdlStream != null) {&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;                    WSDL11ToAxisServiceBuilder&#010;&gt;&gt;wsdl2AxisServiceBuilder&#010;&gt;&gt;                    URL wsdlURL =&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; serviceClassLoader.getResource(wsdlLocation);&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;                    if (wsdlStream == null) {&#010;&gt;&gt; We use the MAP too but generally that's to create&#010;some new artifact.&#010;&#010;Here is the instructions on the MAP site:&#010;&#010;assembly:unpackDeprecated. Use&#010;org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-dependency-plugin goal: unpack or&#010;unpack-dependencies instead.&#010;&#010;I guess my point is...it doesn't matter to me what the plugin is&#010;called...but the plugin that supports unpack today which is MDP should&#010;support AAR too.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;On Tue, Jul 22, 2014 at 9:08 AM, William Ferguson &lt;&#010;william.ferguson@xandar.com.au&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; MDP = maven-dependency-plugin&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; @domi yes you would normally use something like the maven-assembly-plugin&#010;&gt; to disassemble (unpack) an archive.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Wed, Jul 23, 2014 at 12:49 AM, domi &lt;domi@fortysix.ch&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I think to recall a thread on the dev list about plans to remove the&#010;&gt; &gt; unpack goal from the dependency plugin, but I can’t find it anymore…&#010;&gt; &gt; regards Domi&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; On 22.07.2014, at 16:29, William Ferguson &lt;&#010;&gt; william.ferguson@xandar.com.au&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; I totally agree that it makes sense for the dependency plugin to unpack&#010;&gt; &gt; the&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; AAR just like all other archives.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; I just don't understand why you need the MDP to do so.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; On Tue, Jul 22, 2014 at 10:58 PM, David Hoffer &lt;dhoffer6@gmail.com&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt; No that was just an example so I could create a sample project. Name  :- 
&quot;Robert Scholte&quot; &lt;rfscho...@apache.org&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: maven-dependency-plugin unpacking aar format?  
Date  :-
Tue, 22 Jul 2014 17:41:49 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;to be able to unpack/unarchive Maven must know which Unarchiver should be  &#010;used for this type. 'aar' is not one of the few default supported types,  &#010;hence the exception.&#010;The plugin responsible for packaging the aar-file should also have  &#010;configured how to unarchive the aar-file.&#010;In case of dependency:unpack it is quite simple: I would expect that the  &#010;packaging plugin is configured in the pom.xml with a  &#010;&lt;extension&gt;true&lt;/extension&gt;. This way Maven can find such information.&#010;&#010;However, I can imagine that in case of unpack-dependencies the  &#010;aar-project.pom isn't used to detect the corresponding Unarchiver. Sounds  &#010;like an improvement to me.&#010;&#010;thanks,&#010;Robert&#010;&#010;ps. this is also an interesting usecase for the consumer-pom or the  &#010;flatten-maven-plugin&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;Op Mon, 21 Jul 2014 22:40:18 +0200 schreef David Hoffer  &#010;&lt;dhoffer6@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; I'm getting the following error trying to unpack some files from an aar.&#010;&gt;  Is this not supported?  Is there any way to do this?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Failed to execute goal&#010;&gt; org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-dependency-plugin:2.8:unpack-dependencies&#010;&gt; (unpack-service) on project service: Unknown archiver type: No such&#010;&gt; archiver: 'aar'. -&gt; [Help 1]&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; -Dave&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Re: Why not a forum

contents:- 
There is a LinkedIn Maven User group with  2084 members &#010;http://www.linkedin.com/groups?gid=1940051&#010;&#010;It is not as active as it could be but is available for use.&#010;Is a way to have discussions that are easier to manage over a longer term.&#010;&#010;Many of the key resources in this forum are also in the LinkedIn group.&#010;&#010;This has no cost to Apache or any member nor does it require any &#010;additional effort to the PMS or members of the user list to post &#010;questions and discussions (specially if you know how to use copy and paste).&#010;&#010;It does remove a bit of the anonymity of a mailing list but does give &#010;people a chance to look at profiles to judge the experience of the &#010;people asking questions or giving answers.&#010;&#010;It also tracks the influence of people in the group but does not make &#010;that public which would be helpful.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;On 22/07/2014 11:56 AM, Maxim Solodovnik wrote:&#010;&gt; markmail.org is very useful for searching&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 22 July 2014 22:54, Paul Benedict &lt;pbenedict@apache.org&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I think because Apache is a non-profit is cost should be minimal --&#010;&gt;&gt; including cost of time by system administrators. "Apache Policy is that if it didn't happen on the mailing list, it didn't&#010;happen."&#010;&#010;This policy is more important for the dev list where the mailing list is &#010;an integral part of the decision making process and is the official &#010;record of the project.&#010;&#010;For user's, it is not so important.&#010;I currently subscribe here and am one of the 2800 on LinkedIn.&#010;This is a more active place but LinkedIn is going to grow simply because &#010;LinkedIn is already a large group and is part of a larger community with &#010;300 million members.&#010;&#010;It may be a while before the quality of discussion on LinkedIn matches &#010;this mailing list but I would be opposed to supporting any other forum &#010;since 1 mailing list and 1 forum is enough.&#010;&#010;There is no need to pull scarce resources from Apache to build something &#010;from scratch that competes with a Maven group that has 2800 members already.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;On 22/07/2014 4:11 PM, Stephen Connolly wrote:&#010;&gt; Apache Policy is that if it didn't happen on the mailing list, it didn't&#010;&gt; happen.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The ASF *is* mailing lists.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; If you want a forum-like interface there's Nabble...&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Andrew Todd &lt;andrew.todd...@gmail.com&gt;

Re: Re: Why not a forum  
Date  :-
Fri, 25 Jul 2014 14:25:59 GMT  
contents:- 
Apache is an independent non-profit dedicated to the dissemination of free&#010;software. The list archives are freely archivable and indexable by anyone&#010;who wants to -- and there are many sites, such as Nabble and MarkMail, who&#010;do. Using email as the primary means of distribution makes it easy for&#010;third parties to do this.&#010;&#010;On the other hand, LinkedIn is a for-profit corporation with a walled&#010;garden solution. It's "free" because it forces people to tie themselves&#010;into LinkedIn's system. It can't be easily archived or indexed without&#010;LinkedIn's permission. And if they decide to end the service, we're in&#010;trouble.&#010;&#010;There are people like me who will not even create a LinkedIn profile on&#010;principle. I don't like the company's business practices.&#010;&#010;In short, the suggestion is anathema to a free software organization. You&#010;might as well tell us to use Facebook as a discussion medium.&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Jul 23, 2014 at 5:48 PM, Preston, Dale &lt;&#010;Dale.Preston@conocophillips.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I do participate in a couple other Linked-In lists. Stephen Connolly &lt;stephen.alan.conno...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Why not a forum  
Date  :-
Fri, 25 Jul 2014 15:27:13 GMT  
contents:- 
As a member of the Apache Maven PMC, one of my duties is to foster the&#010;community AT Apache. That means the mailing lists.&#010;&#010;If you are looking for an official forum (in the original meaning of the&#010;word) to discuss Maven and its usage, then users@m.a.o is the place to do&#010;that. We cannot stop people who want to discuss Maven elsewhere, nor do we&#010;want to stop them. But we do want to encourage everyone who is discussing&#010;Maven to do so on an Apache hosted mailing list.&#010;&#010;&#010;On 25 July 2014 16:03, Ron Wheeler &lt;rwheeler@artifact-software.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; The Maven group on LinkedIn already has 2090 members and LinkedIn has&#010;&gt; 300,000,000 members.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; There is also a Meven Developers group with 1,083 members.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I support both but I prefer the more modern approach of LinkedIn as a UI.&#010;&gt; I like having all my groups under a single login.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I also support this mailing list even if it is old and has some funny&#010;&gt; interactions with Thunderbird.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have not had any problems with their business practices and find it a&#010;&gt; good way to maintain business contacts and participate in discussions.&#010;&gt; A lot of free and open software are represented in groups on LinkedIn.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I think that you would be hard pressed to find an Apache project that is&#010;&gt; not represented.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; There are 285 LinkedIn groups that show up in a search for Apache.&#010;&gt; Some are very small and inactive and others are larger and active (HADOOP-&#010;&gt; 11,310 members; Distributed Computing (6,241), Mahout 3,894, OpenOffice&#010;&gt; 1358).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; My point is not that everyone should jointhe LinkedIn Maven group but for&#010;&gt; people who don't like mailing lists, there is an alternative that is&#010;&gt; already active.&#010;&gt; There is no need to build another forum.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Ron&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 25/07/2014 10:25 AM, Andrew Todd wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Apache is an independent non-profit dedicated to the dissemination of free&#010;&gt;&gt; software. The list archives are freely archivable and indexable by anyone&#010;&gt;&gt; who wants to -- and there are many sites, such as Nabble and MarkMail, who&#010;&gt;&gt; do. Using email as the primary means of distribution makes it easy for&#010;&gt;&gt; third parties to do this.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; On the other hand, LinkedIn is a for-profit corporation with a walled&#010;&gt;&gt; garden solution. It's "free" because it forces people to tie themselves&#010;&gt;&gt; into LinkedIn's system. It can't be easily archived or indexed without&#010;&gt;&gt; LinkedIn's permission. And if they decide to end the service, we're in&#010;&gt;&gt; trouble.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; There are people like me who will not even create a LinkedIn profile on&#010;&gt;&gt; principle. I don't like the company's business practices.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; In short, the suggestion is anathema to a free software organization. You&#010;&gt;&gt; might as well tell us to use Facebook as a discussion medium.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; On Wed, Jul 23, 2014 at 5:48 PM, Preston, Dale &lt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Dale.Preston@conocophillips.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;  I do participate in a couple other Linked-In lists.  I'll check that one&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; out.  As the response to this thread shows, though, replies come pretty&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; quickly in the email list.  In any case, the Linked-In list sounds worth&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; investigating.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Thanks.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; -----Original Message-----&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; From: Ron Wheeler [mailto:rwheeler@artifact-software.com]&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Sent: Wednesday, July 23, 2014 8:23 AM&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; To: users@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Subject: [EXTERNAL]Re: Why not a forum&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; On 23/07/2014 9:03 AM, Mark H. It seems forum software is more searchable and filterable than&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; email lists.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; If it had been my choice:  because I'd have to go to a forum every day&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; (and a hundred others!) while email comes to me. The list&#010;archives are freely archivable and indexable by anyone who wants to -- and there are many&#010;sites, such as Nabble and MarkMail, who do. Using email as the primary means of distribution&#010;makes it easy for third parties to do this.&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;On the other hand, LinkedIn is a for-profit corporation with a walled garden solution. Re: Upload 3rd party jars retaining original names  
Date  :-
Thu, 24 Jul 2014 11:27:51 GMT  
contents:- 
The name of artifacts in a Maven repo is not possible to specify yourself.&#010;As you've noticed, they are called artifactId-version (and you can also&#010;have a classifier). So no, you cannot give them their "original" name if&#010;that is different from that naming scheme.&#010;&#010;/Anders&#010;&#010;&#010;On Thu, Jul 24, 2014 at 1:20 PM, David Evans &lt;david@evans6.me.uk&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Is it possible to put a bunch of 3rd party jars into a Maven repository&#010;&gt; so that they can be accessed by a project using their original names?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I am developing against a 3rd party software package that includes about&#010;&gt; a dozen supporting jar files. I am trying to upload these jars into a&#010;&gt; Maven repository such that I can put a dependency in my development&#010;&gt; project that puts all of the original jars on my classpath. I have&#010;&gt; tried:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; * insert jars individually (and as a collection) using Nexus console but&#010;&gt; the stored jar is named {artifactId}-{version}&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; * create jar projects with various source structures but, again, the&#010;&gt; stored jar is named {artifactId}-{version}&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; * create a jar project containing an assembly: I can make the 3rd party&#010;&gt; jars visible with their original names but, yet again, they are put into&#010;&gt; in a jar named {artifactId}-{version}.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Context is that I'm just beginning to try and replace historical&#010;&gt; Ant/Eclipse projects with Maven/Eclipse. I've read through "Maven The&#010;&gt; Definitive Guide" and Googled as much as I can but I'm at a stage where&#010;&gt; I'm not even sure I'm asking sensible questions.  If there's a "how to"&#010;&gt; document around (with worked examples rather than isolated XML&#010;&gt; fragments) that would be great.  If I'm missing the point of Maven and&#010;&gt; trying to implement an Ant concept that would be good to know too.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks in advance&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; David&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Hi David,&#010;&#010;&#010; &gt; Is it possible to put a bunch of 3rd party jars into a Maven repository&#010;&gt; so that they can be accessed by a project using their original names?&#010;&#010;What do you mean by original names? As they were in Ant? More or simple &#010;answer to this is no, cause Maven has it's rules how artifacts are &#010;stored in a repository.&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I am developing against a 3rd party software package that includes about&#010;&gt; a dozen supporting jar files. I am trying to upload these jars into a&#010;&gt; Maven repository such that I can put a dependency in my development&#010;&gt; project that puts all of the original jars on my classpath. I have&#010;&gt; tried:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; * insert jars individually (and as a collection) using Nexus console but&#010;&gt; the stored jar is named {artifactId}-{version}&#010;This is the rule as artifacts are stored in a repository...&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; * create jar projects with various source structures but, again, the&#010;&gt; stored jar is named {artifactId}-{version}&#010;The sources structure is not related to the naming rules, cause you &#010;should think about how would other consume those artifacts if they do &#010;not follow a naming rule...big example see Maven Central....&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; * create a jar project containing an assembly: I can make the 3rd party&#010;&gt; jars visible with their original names but, yet again, they are put into&#010;&gt; in a jar named {artifactId}-{version}.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Context is that I'm just beginning to try and replace historical&#010;&gt; Ant/Eclipse projects with Maven/Eclipse. I've read through "Maven The&#010;&gt; Definitive Guide" and Googled as much as I can but I'm at a stage where&#010;&gt; I'm not even sure I'm asking sensible questions.  If there's a "how to"&#010;&gt; document around (with worked examples rather than isolated XML&#010;&gt; fragments) that would be great.  If I'm missing the point of Maven and&#010;&gt; trying to implement an Ant concept that would be good to know too.&#010;&#010;You have to follow the naming rule and change other projects to consume &#010;those artifacts with the appropriate naming rules....&#010;&#010;Kind regards&#010;Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Maven?&#010;&#010;Way too much work!&#010;This appears to be a normal case that Maven will handle without any fuss.&#010;Have a look at the Maven articles and books.&#010;&#010;If you are building something that is very common and do not have any &#010;truly bizarre development processes, then Maven should be able to handle &#010;your process in a simple way.&#010;&#010;The danger of asking very detailed questions here without providing &#010;context is that there are very smart and creative people in this forum &#010;who can make Maven do damn-near anything.&#010;They might take your question a bit too literally and actually provide a &#010;very elegant solution to a problem that is only slightly misstated.&#010;&#010;&gt; You cannot conditionally trigger one profile from within the other. You&#010;will need to have two separate ones.&#010;&#010;&#010;On Thu, Jul 24, 2014 at 6:17 PM, hanuman &lt;hanumannallapati@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; thanks very much(martin and brend) for your prompt replies .&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; i.e.., can I conditionally invoke a profile within the other profile?&#010;&gt;                      or&#010;&gt; create a two profiles and run a separate command for each of them?&#010;&gt;   ex: mvn -Pcreate-profile1 -e            (to execute script1 and script2&#010;&gt; .sql)&#010;&gt;        mvn -Pcreate-profile2 -e            (to execute script3.sql)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context:&#010;&gt; http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Conditionally-executing-a-script-in-profile-tp5800947p5800950.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;
